# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Analyze Test Coverage Gaps in Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) filter chain implementation. The HCM is the core HTTP processing pipeline in Envoy, responsible for routing, filter execution, and response handling.

## Scope

Focus on the HCM implementation in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` and its test file `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc`. Also consider:
- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — filter chain execution
- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — header manipulation

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific untested code paths** in the HCM (with file + approximate line references)
2. **Propose a concrete test case** for each gap (test name, setup, assertions)
3. **Explain why each gap matters** (what bugs could slip through)
4. **Prioritize by risk**: label each gap as HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md` with this structure:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary
[Brief overview of the most critical gaps found]

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: [Title]
- **File**: source/common/http/...
- **Lines**: ~NNN-NNN
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Description**: [What code path is untested]
- **Proposed Test**: [Test name and approach]
- **Why It Matters**: [Potential bugs if untested]

[Repeat for gaps 2-5+]

## File References
[List of key files analyzed]
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate file paths or function names — inspect the actual codebase
- Do not list gaps without proposing concrete test cases

123-assistanttext-
The analysis has been written to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`. Here's a summary of what was found:

---

## 5 Coverage Gaps Identified

**Gap 1 — Premature Reset Early-Drain Prediction (HIGH)**
`conn_manager_impl.cc:~727–738` — `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` has a two-branch heuristic: it drains the connection *early* when the reset-to-total ratio predicts the limit will eventually be exceeded, even before the configured stream count threshold is hit. Neither branch is tested. The `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` recursion guard is also untested. A regression here allows abusive clients to issue hundreds of premature resets without triggering connection teardown.

**Gap 2 — Encoder Filter Removes `:status` → 502 (HIGH)**
`filter_manager.cc:~1323–1336` — After the encoder filter chain runs, `checkRequiredResponseHeaders()` catches a missing/invalid `:status` and sends a 502. The `HeaderUtility` function is unit-tested in isolation, but there is no integration test in any `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` that drives an encoder filter to delete the header and confirms the client receives a 502. An unchecked regression silently produces protocol violations at the codec.

**Gap 3 — HTTP/3 Deferred Access Logging (MEDIUM)**
`conn_manager_impl.cc:~362–375` — On HTTP/3 streams without a downstream reset, `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` skips `log(DownstreamEnd)` and calls `deferHeadersAndTrailers()` to hand logging to the QUIC ACK listener. All four required conditions (HTTP/3 protocol, no downstream reset, live encoder, runtime flag) are never simultaneously true in any existing test. A regression means silent loss of HTTP/3 access logs.

**Gap 4 — Route-Level Idle Timeout = 0 Disables Global Timer (MEDIUM)**
`conn_manager_impl.cc:~2355–2379` — A route-configured idle timeo
... (truncated)

  "content": "# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nAnalysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`, `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`, and their test files reveals several meaningful coverage gaps. The most critical is the **premature-reset early-drain prediction logic**, which has a subtle math condition that could allow abusive clients to avoid connection termination. Also critical is the **missing integration test for encoder filter corrupting response status** \u2014 a 502 path that exists in `filter_manager.cc` but has never been triggered through the full HCM stack. Several timer/lifecycle edge cases in `ActiveStream` are also absent.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature Reset Early-Drain Prediction Logic\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~727\u2013738\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` has two distinct code branches depending on whether the total stream count has reached the configured limit (default 500). The *below-limit* branch (lines 727\u2013733) implements an early-drain heuristic: even if `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, Envoy drains the connection early when `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit`. This predicts that, even if all future streams are good, the reset ratio will still exceed 50% by the time the limit is reached. The *above-limit* branch (lines 734\u2013738) checks `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_`. No test exercises either computation path; searching all `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` files finds zero occurrences of `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_`, `PrematureReset`, or `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, PrematureResetEarlyDrainPrediction)` \u2014 configure `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey` to 10 and `PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey` to 1. Issue 6 streams that each reset within 1 second without a response (premature). After the 6th stream destroy, `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 = 12 >= 10 = limit`, so the early-drain should fire. Assert:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value() == 1`\n  - Connection is closed via `Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort`\n  - A second call to `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` (simulated by calling destroy on another stream) does NOT increment the stat again, proving the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` guard works.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The early-drain threshold is meant to stop slow-drip reset attacks before they reach the full limit. An off-by-one error in the `* 2` heuristic could allow a client to issue hundreds of premature resets without triggering connection termination. The recursion guard (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) prevents a stack overflow described in the comment, but it is also untested \u2014 a regression could cause infinite recursion and crash the proxy.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Encoder Filter Removes `:status` Header \u2014 502 BadGateway Path\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1323\u20131336\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: After the encoder filter chain processes response headers, `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` calls `HeaderUtility::checkRequiredResponseHeaders(headers)`. If the `:status` header is missing or non-numeric (e.g., an encoder filter removed it or set it to a non-integer), the code calls `sendLocalReply(Http::Code::BadGateway, \u2026)` with the details string `FilterRemovedRequiredResponseHeaders{\u2026}`. The `header_utility_test.cc` tests `HeaderUtility::checkRequiredResponseHeaders` in isolation, but there is no test in any `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` that creates an encoder filter which removes `:status` and then verifies the client receives a 502.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, EncoderFilterRemovesStatusHeader502)` \u2014 set up a decoder+encoder filter chain with one encoder filter whose `encodeHeaders()` removes the `:status` header and returns `FilterHeadersStatus::Continue`. Fire a normal request, trigger a 200 response from the decoder filter. Assert:\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(response_encoder_, encodeHeaders(HasStatus(\"502\"), true))` is invoked (the sendLocalReply path bypasses the filter chain).\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_5xx_.value() == 1`.\n  - `stream_info.responseCodeDetails()` contains `FilterRemovedRequiredResponseHeaders`.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: An encoder filter with a bug (or a malicious one) that erases the `:status` header currently silently bypasses the response \u2014 the codec would receive a response with no `:status`, which is a protocol violation causing undefined behavior at the codec level. The 502 guard was added specifically to prevent this, but without a test it is easy to accidentally regress (e.g., by changing the check order in `encodeHeaders()`).\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: HTTP/3 Deferred Access Logging (`deferHeadersAndTrailers`)\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~362\u2013375\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: In `doDeferredStreamDestroy()`, there is a branch specifically for HTTP/3 streams (when `codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3`) that skips the usual `stream.log(DownstreamEnd)` call and instead calls `stream.deferHeadersAndTrailers()` to hand off logging to the QUIC ACK listener. This path is gated by:\n  1. `codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3`\n  2. `!stream.filter_manager_.sawDownstreamReset()`\n  3. `stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr`\n  4. The `envoy.reloadable_features.quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener` runtime flag is true\n\n  None of the existing `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` tests exercises this path with all four conditions true. Existing HTTP/3 tests only verify codec creation stats; they do not verify deferred logging behavior.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, Http3DeferredAccessLoggingOnStreamComplete)` \u2014 use `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, protocol()).WillRepeatedly(Return(Protocol::Http3))`, enable `quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener`, and attach a mock access logger. Process a normal request-response cycle without downstream reset. Assert:\n  - The access logger's `log()` method is NOT called with `DownstreamEnd` type during stream destroy (logging is deferred).\n  - `stream.deferHeadersAndTrailers()` stores the headers/trailers on the stream object (inspectable via a mock or subclass).\n  - If a downstream reset occurs on the same stream configuration, `log(DownstreamEnd)` IS called immediately (verifying the `!sawDownstreamReset()` guard).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: HTTP/3's deferred logging is intended to report accurate timing by waiting for QUIC ACK. If this code path is broken (e.g., `deferHeadersAndTrailers` never transfers state), HTTP/3 connections will silently produce no access logs for successful requests. The runtime flag path also means this could regress silently when the flag is promoted to default-on.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Route-Level Idle Timeout = 0 Explicitly Disables Global Stream Timer\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2355\u20132379 (`refreshIdleAndFlushTimeouts`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `refreshIdleAndFlushTimeouts()` (called from `setVirtualHostRoute()` on every route cache update) handles the case where a route-level idle timeout of exactly 0 is configured to mean \"no timeout\" \u2014 overriding the global HCM stream idle timeout. Lines 2364\u20132368 show: if the global idle timer exists (`stream_idle_timer_ != nullptr`) but the route says 0, the timer is disabled and nulled out. Separately, lines 2372\u20132379 implement `setFlushTimeout` inheritance: if there is no explicit route flush timeout *and* the global flush timeout was inherited from the global idle timeout (`!has_explicit_global_flush_timeout_`), then the route idle timeout is also used as the flush timeout. Neither of these sub-paths appears in any test; searches for `idleTimeout` combined with stream timer interactions in the test files only find the positive (non-zero) timeout cases.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, RouteLevelIdleTimeoutZeroDisablesGlobalTimer)` \u2014 configure a global `streamIdleTimeout` of 10s. For the request's matching route, configure `idleTimeout = 0` (no timeout). After `decodeHeaders()` processes the request (triggering `setVirtualHostRoute`), assert that `stream_idle_timer_` is null (the global timer was disabled). Then simulate time passing past 10s and verify no idle timeout fires. Contrast with a control test where the route has no `idleTimeout` override, and the timer remains active.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Route-level timeout overrides are an operator-facing configuration knob. If the `== 0` condition silently fails to disable the timer, every request matching that route would still be subject to the global idle timeout \u2014 a subtle misconfiguration that would be very hard to diagnose. The flush timeout inheritance path (`!has_explicit_global_flush_timeout_`) is also complex; if broken, stream flush behavior diverges from expectations when only `idleTimeout` is set on a route.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: HTTP/2 Trailer Validation \u2014 Underscore Headers Reset Rather Than 400\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1256\u20131300 (`validateTrailers`)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: `validateTrailers()` handles the case where a request trailer fails UHV validation. # Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary

Analysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`, `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`, and their test files reveals several meaningful coverage gaps. The most critical is the **premature-reset early-drain prediction logic**, which has a subtle math condition that could allow abusive clients to avoid connection termination. Also critical is the **missing integration test for encoder filter corrupting response status** — a 502 path that exists in `filter_manager.cc` but has never been triggered through the full HCM stack. Several timer/lifecycle edge cases in `ActiveStream` are also absent.

---

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: Premature Reset Early-Drain Prediction Logic

- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`
- **Lines**: ~727–738
- **Risk**: HIGH
- **Description**: `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` has two distinct code branches depending on whether the total stream count has reached the configured limit (default 500). The *below-limit* branch (lines 727–733) implements an early-drain heuristic: even if `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, Envoy drains the connection early when `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit`. This predicts that, even if all future streams are good, the reset ratio will still exceed 50% by the time the limit is reached. The *above-limit* branch (lines 734–738) checks `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_`. No test exercises either computation path; searching all `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` files finds zero occurrences of `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_`, `PrematureReset`, or `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`.
